This system comprises four images in the observer plane with a maximum separation of \u223c 6<SUP>\\prime\\prime</SUP> and it is lensed by a z=0.55 massive early-type galaxy. It was initially identified in the Baryon Oscillation Spectroscopic Survey Emission-Line Lens Survey for GALaxy-Ly\u03b1 EmitteR sYstems survey, and follow-up imaging and spectroscopic observations using the Gran Telescopio Canarias and William Herschel Telescope confirmed the lensing nature of this system. A lens model using a singular isothermal ellipsoid in an external shear field reproduces the main features of the system quite well, yielding an Einstein radius of 2.\u203395 \u00b1 0.\u203310, and a total magnification factor for the LAE of 8.8 \u00b1 0.4. This LAE is one of the brightest and most luminous galaxy-galaxy strong lenses known. We present initial imaging and spectroscopy showing the basic physical and morphological properties of this lensed system. <P />Based on observations made with the Gran Telescopio Canarias (GTC) and William Herschel Telescope (WHT), in the Spanish Observatorio del Roque de los Muchachos of the IAC, under Directors Discretionary Time (DDT programs IDs: GTC2016-054 and DDT2016-077).", "doi": <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Joel R. Brownstein</span><a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://orcid.org/0000-0002-8725-1069\" title=\"https://orcid.org/0000-0002-8725-1069\"><svg xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg\" viewBox=\"0 0 256 256\" width=\"20\" class=\"orcid-logo\"><path class=\"st0\" d=\"M256 128c0 70.7-57.3 128-128 128C57.3 256 0 198.7 0 128 0 57.3 57.3 0 128 0 198.7 End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">2041-8205/834/2/L18</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n            <P>We report the discovery of a very bright (<I>r</I>\u00a0=\u00a020.16), highly magnified, and yet intrinsically very luminous Ly<I>\u03b1</I> emitter (LAE) at <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$z=2.82$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/apjlaa5591ieqn1.gif\"></IMG>. This system comprises four images in the observer plane with a maximum separation of <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$\\sim 6^{\\prime\\prime} $\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/apjlaa5591ieqn2.gif\"></IMG> and it is lensed by a <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$z=0.55$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/apjlaa5591ieqn3.gif\"></IMG> massive early-type galaxy. It was initially identified in the Baryon Oscillation Spectroscopic Survey Emission-Line Lens Survey for GALaxy-Ly<I>\u03b1</I> EmitteR sYstems survey, and follow-up imaging and spectroscopic observations using the Gran Telescopio Canarias and William Herschel Telescope confirmed the lensing nature of this system. A lens model using a singular isothermal ellipsoid in an external shear field reproduces the main features of the system quite well, yielding an Einstein radius of 2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />95\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />10, and a total magnification factor for the LAE of 8.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.4. This LAE is one of the brightest and most luminous galaxy\u2013galaxy strong lenses known. We present initial imaging and spectroscopy showing the basic physical and morphological properties of this lensed system.</P></div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=2041-8205/834/2/L18&doi=10.3847/2041-8213/834/2/L18&exportFormat=iopexport_bib&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-bib\" title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=2041-8205/834/2/L18&doi=10.3847/2041-8213/834/2/L18&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-ris\" title=\"Export RIS\">RIS</a>\n\t\t</span>\n\t</p>\n<!-- End Export citation and abstract tools -->\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2017ApJ...834L..18M\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://nedwww.ipac.caltech.edu/cgi-bin/nph-objsearch?refcode=2017ApJ...834L..18M&search_type=Search \" target=\"_blank\">NED Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2017ApJ...834L..18M\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/2041-8205/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa5591s1\" name=\"apjlaa5591s1\">1.\u00a0Introduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The study of the physical properties of typical <em>L</em>* high-redshift galaxies has been limited by their faintness (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn4.gif\" alt=\"$r\\simeq 24.5$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">r\\simeq 24.5</script></span></span> at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn5.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span>), even for 8/10 m class telescopes. Recently, the properties of these high-redshift galaxies have been studied by building large samples of hundreds to thousands of individual spectra to construct high signal-to-noise ratio (S/N) composite spectra (e.g., Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib32\">2003</a>). Although these techniques have been very successful, they require a large amount of observing time and only probe the average physical properties of these galaxies. Another way to study high-redshift galaxies in detail is to use the fortuitous alignments with foreground massive structures, which provide natural magnification and associated amplification produced by strong gravitational lensing. Hundreds of strongly lensed galaxies have recently been discovered by employing various observational techniques, mainly from the optical to the radio. However, only a handful of optically very bright (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn6.gif\" alt=\"$r\\sim 20$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">r\\sim 20</script></span></span>), strongly magnified high-redshift galaxies have been discovered so far (Yee et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib41\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib41\">1996</a>; Allam et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib1\">2007</a>; Belokurov et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib2\">2007</a>; Smail et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib37\">2007</a>; Lin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib17\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib17\">2009</a>; Dahle et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib9\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib9\">2016</a>), allowing detailed spectroscopic studies of their individual properties, such as stellar populations, chemical composition, and kinematics of the interstellar medium (e.g., Pettini et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib24\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib24\">2000</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib23\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib23\">2002</a>; Quider et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib25\">2009</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib26\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib26\">2010</a>; Dessauges-Zavadsky et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib11\">2010</a>).</p><p>In this Letter, we report the discovery of a bright (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn7.gif\" alt=\"$r\\sim 20$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">r\\sim 20</script></span></span>), quadruply gravitationally lensed Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emitter (LAE). We provide the first physical and morphological analysis of the lensing galaxy and the lensed LAE. Throughout the Letter, we adopt a cosmology with <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn8.gif\" alt=\"${{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{m}}}=0.274$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{m}}}=0.274</script></span></span>, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn9.gif\" alt=\"${{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{\\Lambda }}}=0.726$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{\\Lambda }}}=0.726</script></span></span> and <em>H</em><sub><em>o</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a070 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. All quoted magnitudes are in the AB system.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa5591s2\" name=\"apjlaa5591s2\">2.\u00a0Discovery and Follow-up</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Recently, by searching for secondary emission lines in the spectra of massive elliptical galaxies within the database of the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS: York et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib42\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib42\">2000</a>), the Sloan Lens ACS Survey (SLACS: e.g., Bolton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib5\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib5\">2006</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib4\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib4\">2008</a>), and the Baryon Oscillation Spectroscopic Survey (BOSS) Emission-Line Lens Survey (BELLS: Brownstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib6\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib6\">2012</a>) have discovered over 100 lensed star-forming galaxies at moderate redshifts (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn10.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 1$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 1</script></span></span>). Very recently, by applying spectroscopic selection techniques similar to SLACS and BELLS, but adapted to high-redshift Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission, Shu et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib34\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib34\">2016a</a>) identified a new sample of 187 high-probability lensed LAE candidate systems at 2 &lt; <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn11.gif\" alt=\"${z}_{\\mathrm{LAE}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{z}_{\\mathrm{LAE}}</script></span></span> &lt; 3, the BOSS Emission-Line Lens Survey for GALaxy-Ly<em>\u03b1</em> EmitteR sYstems (BELLS GALLERY) survey, selected from the final data release (DR12) of the BOSS (Dawson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib10\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib10\">2013</a>) of the SDSS-III (Eisenstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib12\">2011</a>). Of these, 21 of the highest quality candidates were recently observed with the <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> and the first results were presented in Shu et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib35\">2016b</a>).</p><p>By visual inspection of SDSS and DECaLS<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa5591fn2\">12</a></sup>\n color images of the BELLS GALLERY sample, we found one candidate showing bluish features <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />3<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />3 from the <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn12.gif\" alt=\"$z=0.5531$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=0.5531</script></span></span> massive early-type galaxy, SDSS J142954.80+120235.6 (hereafter ETG). Its BOSS spectrum (Plate-MJD-Fiber: 5463-56003-121) shows a secondary emission line at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn13.gif\" alt=\"$4652\\,\\mathring{\\rm A} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">4652\\,\\mathring{\\rm A}</script></span></span> (Ly<em>\u03b1</em> at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn14.gif\" alt=\"$z=2.8253;$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2.8253;</script></span></span> Shu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib34\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib34\">2016a</a>). The positions of the bluish features with respect to the ETG are consistent with a <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn15.gif\" alt=\"${\\text{}}{fold}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\text{}}{fold}</script></span></span> lensing configuration: a bright lensed image pair, A and B (with a separation of <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5), and two fainter images, C and D (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>). The lensed image pair, A and B, is identified in SDSS as a single source, SDSS J142954.88+120238.3 (hereafter BG1429+1202 for the lensed LAE, where BG stands for BELLS GALLERY), showing blue colors in the DECaLS and SDSS bands (Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjlaa5591t1\">1</a>). The lensed A and B images are also detected in the UKIRT Infrared Deep Sky\u00a0 Large Area Survey (Lawrence et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib16\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib16\">2007</a>), only in the <em>Y</em>-band with 21.06\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.19 mag and 21.12\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.20 mag, respectively.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjlaa5591f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjlaa5591f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img artifacts in DECaLS co-adds, and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">(5)</script></span></span> the lensed images A and B were deblended using <span class=\"small-caps\">GALFIT</span> (Peng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib22\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib22\">2002</a>). The magnitudes listed have not been corrected for the Galactic dust extinction, which are 0.104, 0.072, and 0.040 mag for <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, and <em>z</em>, respectively (Schlafly &amp; Finkbeiner <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib30\">2011</a>).</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/suppdata/apjlaa5591t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/2041-8213/834/2/L18\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/suppdata/apjlaa5591t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>We carried out Director Discretionary Time (DDT) for optical imaging and long-slit spectroscopic observations on 2016 June 29 using the Auxiliary-port Camera (ACAM: Benn et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib3\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib3\">2008</a>) at the William Herschel Telescope (WHT) to confirm the lensing nature of this LAE. The ACAM long-slit was oriented at a sky position angle (PA)\u00a0=\u00a0<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn32.gif\" alt=\"$103\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 35$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">103\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 35</script></span></span>, and positioned so as to encompass the two brightest lensed images, A and B, as shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>. Despite the bad seeing conditions that night (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn33.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim 4^{\\prime\\prime} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim 4^{\\prime\\prime}</script></span></span> FWHM), we could confirm the lensing nature of this system with the detection in the long-slit spectrum of strong rest-frame UV continuum (with Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> and C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> in absorption) and Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission at a redshift <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn34.gif\" alt=\"$z=2.823\\pm 0.008$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2.823\\pm 0.008</script></span></span>, in agreement with the redshift of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> detected in the BOSS fiber spectrum, likely from the lensed image D (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>).</p><p>We again observed BG1429+1202 on 2016 July 29, this time in very good seeing conditions (<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />75 FWHM, measured in the 330 s <em>g</em>-band acquisition image), using the Optical System for Imaging and low-Intermediate-Resolution Integrated Spectroscopy camera (OSIRIS<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa5591fn3\">13</a></sup>\n) on the Gran Telescopio Canarias (GTC). We used the R1000B grism, which provides a spectral coverage of 3630\u20137500 \u00c5 (950\u20131960 \u00c5, rest-frame) and a dispersion of 2.12 \u00c5 px<sup>\u22121</sup>. The OSIRIS <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn35.gif\" alt=\"$1\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 2</script></span></span> wide long-slit was oriented in the same PA used in the WHT/ACAM spectroscopic observations (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>). Given this configuration, the corresponding spectral resolution is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn36.gif\" alt=\"$\\simeq 8\\,\\mathring{\\rm A} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\simeq 8\\,\\mathring{\\rm A}</script></span></span> (or <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn37.gif\" alt=\"$\\simeq 500$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\simeq 500</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup> FWHM). The total integration time was 44 minutes, split into 4\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a0660 s. The data were reduced with <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span> and <span class=\"small-caps\">python</span> tasks.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa5591s3\" name=\"apjlaa5591s3\">3.\u00a0Analysis and Discussion</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjlaa5591s3-1\" name=\"apjlaa5591s3-1\">3.1.\u00a0Source Properties</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The rest-frame UV spectrum of the brightest lensed images, A and B, is shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f2\">2</a>. Despite the relatively short exposure time, the achieved high S/N GTC/OSIRIS spectrum (~25 in the continuum) shows a strong Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission, and a series of strong absorption lines, similar to those seen in the composite spectrum of hundreds of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn38.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> Lyman break galaxies (LBGs) (Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib32\">2003</a>). The strongest absorption features are associated with the interstellar medium and stellar winds in a variety of ionization states, from neutral (O <span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>) to highly ionized species (Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> or C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>). High ionization features with a strong P Cygni profile are seen both in C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn39.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1548$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1548</script></span></span>, 1550 and Al <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn40.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1854$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1854</script></span></span>, 1862 doublets, which is indicative of stellar winds from very young massive stars. However, we identify additional absorption features unrelated to BG1429+1202 (nine absorption features associated with an intervening metal-line system at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn41.gif\" alt=\"${z}_{\\mathrm{abs}}=2.179\\pm 0.001$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{z}_{\\mathrm{abs}}=2.179\\pm 0.001</script></span></span>, and one broad absorption line at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn42.gif\" alt=\"$5183\\,\\mathring{\\rm A} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">5183\\,\\mathring{\\rm A}</script></span></span> with an observed equivalent width <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn43.gif\" alt=\"${W}_{\\mathrm{obs}}=6.95\\pm 0.2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{W}_{\\mathrm{obs}}=6.95\\pm 0.2</script></span></span> \u00c5 remains unidentified). Analysis of the spectra for the individual lensed images A and B shows no differences in the profiles of the absorption features and no evidence for velocity offsets between them, as expected if they are both images of the same background source. The same happens to their rest-frame UV slope, <em>\u03b2</em>, which is essentially flat in <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn44.gif\" alt=\"${F}_{\\nu }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{F}_{\\nu }</script></span></span>. Adopting a simple power-law approximation for the UV spectral range <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn45.gif\" alt=\"${F}_{\\lambda }\\propto {\\lambda }^{\\beta }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{F}_{\\lambda }\\propto {\\lambda }^{\\beta }</script></span></span> and using the observed <em>r</em> and <em>z</em> magnitudes (~1600\u20132400 \u00c5 rest-frame), we derive <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn46.gif\" alt=\"$\\beta =-2.1\\pm 0.1$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\beta =-2.1\\pm 0.1</script></span></span>, which implies an effective UV extinction <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn47.gif\" alt=\"${A}_{1600}\\sim 0.6$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{A}_{1600}\\sim 0.6</script></span></span> or <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn48.gif\" alt=\"$E(B-V)\\sim 0.13$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)\\sim 0.13</script></span></span>, reflecting modest dust content (Calzetti et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib7\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib7\">2000</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjlaa5591f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjlaa5591f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591f2_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div 2.</strong>\u00a0GTC/OSIRIS spectrum of BG1429+1202 (black solid line) and its <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn49.gif\" alt=\"$1\\sigma $\" The 2D spectrum is also shown on the top. In the inset panel we show the BOSS and WHT spectra with the positions of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission, as well as the absorption features related to the ETG at <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span from the BOSS fiber spectrum.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjlaa5591f2\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/downloadFigure/figure/apjlaa5591f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjlaa5591f2\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjlaa5591f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>We identified several photospheric absorption features, from which we derived the systemic redshift <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn51.gif\" alt=\"${z}_{\\mathrm{sys}}=2.8224\\,\\pm \\,0.0013$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{z}_{\\mathrm{sys}}=2.8224\\,\\pm \\,0.0013</script></span></span> using the cleanest among them: O <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn52.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1343$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1343</script></span></span>, and a close blend of C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and N <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span> at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn53.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1324$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1324</script></span></span>.</p><p>The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission line has an observed (A + B) flux of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn54.gif\" alt=\"${F}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=(2.1\\pm 0.3)\\times {10}^{-15}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{F}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=(2.1\\pm 0.3)\\times {10}^{-15}</script></span></span> erg s<sup>\u22121</sup> cm<sup>\u22122</sup>, much higher than the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> flux measured within the <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn55.gif\" alt=\"$1^{\\prime\\prime} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1^{\\prime\\prime}</script></span></span>-radius BOSS fiber (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn56.gif\" alt=\"${F}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{\\mathrm{BOSS}}=0.256\\times {10}^{-15}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{F}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{\\mathrm{BOSS}}=0.256\\times {10}^{-15}</script></span></span> erg s<sup>\u22121</sup> cm<sup>\u22122</sup>). The measured rest-frame equivalent width of Ly<em>\u03b1</em> is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn57.gif\" alt=\"${W}_{0}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=39\\pm 15$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{W}_{0}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=39\\pm 15</script></span></span> \u00c5. The errors reflect the uncertainty in the determination of the stellar continuum redward of Ly<em>\u03b1</em>. Although the line appears unresolved in our low-resolution spectrum (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn58.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{FWHM}\\simeq 500$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{FWHM}\\simeq 500</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup>), it is resolved in the BOSS spectrum. Fitting a Gaussian to the BOSS Ly<em>\u03b1</em> line, we measured a FWHM of 382\u00a0\u00b1\u00a050 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, after accounting for the instrumental broadening. The nebular C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii]</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn59.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1906$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1906</script></span></span>, 1908 doublet is also detected in emission but with low significance (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn60.gif\" alt=\"$4\\sigma $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">4\\sigma</script></span></span>) and is not resolved in our GTC/OSIRIS spectrum. This galaxy can be classified as an LAE, given the rest-frame equivalent width and the velocity width of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> line (e.g., Ouchi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib20\">2008</a>). From our spectrum and available photometric data we do not detect evidence of any AGN contribution. However, a more extensive characterization awaits higher spatial resolution imaging and multi-wavelength photometry.</p><p>A careful analysis of the kinematics goes beyond the present Letter given the low spectral resolution of these data. However, the high S/N of the GTC/OSIRIS spectrum allows us to detect differences in the kinematics of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission and interstellar features. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f3\">3</a> (left panel) shows velocity plots of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission line and several normalized interstellar absorption lines, relative to <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn61.gif\" alt=\"${z}_{\\mathrm{sys}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{z}_{\\mathrm{sys}}</script></span></span>. The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission has its peak redshifted with a velocity <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn62.gif\" alt=\"${v}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim +200$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{v}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim +200</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, while the interstellar absorption lines appear blueshifted by <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn63.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim -150$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim -150</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, which is consistent with galaxy-scale outflows of material from the galaxy in the form of a wind, similar to those seen in other star-forming galaxies at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn64.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> (Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib32\">2003</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjlaa5591f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjlaa5591f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591f3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\"
