size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0Left: GTC/OSIRIS and BOSS Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission (upper panel) and interstellar absorption features (lower panel) on rest velocity frame. The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission appears to be redshifted, <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn65.gif\" alt=\"${v}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim +200$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{v}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim +200</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, while the interstellar absorption lines are blueshifted by <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn66.gif\" alt=\"${v}_{\\mathrm{abs}}\\sim -150$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{v}_{\\mathrm{abs}}\\sim -150</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup> (mean profile in black with the standard deviation in gray shadow). Right: 2D Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission in the position\u2013velocity plane (upper panel) where a spatial gradient of velocity is seen in both A and B images. In the lower panel we show the normalized spatial profiles of the rest-frame UV continuum (green line) and Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission (blue line). The shaded regions show the <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn67.gif\" alt=\"$1\\sigma $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1\\sigma</script></span></span> errors of the spatial profiles. The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission appears more extended between A and B than the rest-frame UV continuum.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjlaa5591f3\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/downloadFigure/figure/apjlaa5591f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjlaa5591f3\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjlaa5591f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>We also notice that a spatial gradient of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> velocity is present in the 2D spectrum (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f3\">3</a>, right upper panel). This velocity structure is seen both in A and B but appears mirrored, as expected for those images in this system, as A and B images straddle the fold critical curve (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>). We carefully checked the 2D spectrum to see if this pattern is present in other lines, but we found none with this signature. The 1D spatial distribution of Ly<em>\u03b1</em> is also compared with that of the rest-frame UV continuum (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f3\">3</a>, right lower panel). The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission appears more extended in the inner region between A and B, than the UV continuum. Deeper and higher spatial resolution observations are needed to constrain the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> and UV continuum spatial distributions.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjlaa5591s3-2\" name=\"apjlaa5591s3-2\">3.2.\u00a0Lens Model</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>To interpret the properties of the lensed system in more detail, we used the 330 s GTC/OSIRIS <em>g</em>-band image obtained in <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn68.gif\" alt=\"$\\simeq 0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 75$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\simeq 0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 75</script></span></span> FWHM seeing for accurate lens modeling. As shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>, the lens system comprises four images forming a so-called <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn69.gif\" alt=\"${\\text{}}{fold}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\text{}}{fold}</script></span></span> configuration, when the source lies very close to a <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn70.gif\" alt=\"${\\text{}}{fold}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\text{}}{fold}</script></span></span> caustic. Similar to previous works (Bolton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib4\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib4\">2008</a>; Brownstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib6\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib6\">2012</a>; Shu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib33\">2015</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib35\">2016b</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib36\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib36\">2016c</a>), we have developed a lens model using a nonlinear optimizer, consisting of minimizing a <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn71.gif\" alt=\"${\\chi }^{2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\chi }^{2}</script></span></span> function using the Levenberg\u2013Marquardt algorithm with the <tt>LMFIT</tt> package (Newville et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib19\">2014</a>), where the observational data are compared to the model (see Shu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib35\">2016b</a> for details). The foreground-light is modeled using the elliptical S\u00e9rsic profile and similar to Shu et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib33\">2015</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib35\">2016b</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib36\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib36\">2016c</a>), its subtraction is performed jointly with the lens modeling. The lens model includes a mass distribution of the foreground lens parameterized as a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE), and an additional external shear is included to model the higher-order effect from the environment. The surface brightness distribution of the background source is reconstructed parametrically using an elliptical S\u00e9rsic model. The foreground-light model is combined with the predicted lensed images and convolved with the point-spread function that was modeled with a star in the GTC/OSIRIS <em>g</em>-band field of view.</p><p>For the lens, the best-fit lens model (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn72.gif\" alt=\"${\\chi }^{2}/\\mathrm{dof}=3494/3709$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\chi }^{2}/\\mathrm{dof}=3494/3709</script></span></span>) predicts an Einstein radius <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn73.gif\" alt=\"${b}_{\\mathrm{SIE}}=2\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 95\\,\\pm \\,0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 10$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{b}_{\\mathrm{SIE}}=2\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 95\\,\\pm \\,0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 10</script></span></span>, a minor-to-major axis ratio <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn74.gif\" alt=\"$q=0.34$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">q=0.34</script></span></span>, and a position angle <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn75.gif\" alt=\"${\\rm{P}}.{\\rm{A}}.\\,=\\,165\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 5$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\rm{P}}.{\\rm{A}}.\\,=\\,165\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 5</script></span></span>. The strength and position angle of the external shear are <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn76.gif\" alt=\"$\\gamma =0.059\\pm 0.008$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\gamma =0.059\\pm 0.008</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn77.gif\" alt=\"${\\phi }_{\\gamma }=89\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 9$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\phi }_{\\gamma }=89\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 9</script></span></span>, respectively. The characteristic lensing velocity dispersion defined as <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn78.gif\" alt=\"${\\sigma }_{\\mathrm{SIE}}=c\\sqrt{\\tfrac{{b}_{\\mathrm{SIE}}}{4\\pi }\\tfrac{{D}_{{\\rm{L}}}}{{D}_{\\mathrm{LS}}}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\sigma }_{\\mathrm{SIE}}=c\\sqrt{\\tfrac{{b}_{\\mathrm{SIE}}}{4\\pi }\\tfrac{{D}_{{\\rm{L}}}}{{D}_{\\mathrm{LS}}}}</script></span></span> is 390\u00a0\u00b1\u00a06 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, where <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn79.gif\" alt=\"${D}_{\\mathrm{LS}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{D}_{\\mathrm{LS}}</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn80.gif\" alt=\"${D}_{{\\rm{S}}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{D}_{{\\rm{S}}}</script></span></span> are the angular diameter distances from the lens and the observer to the source, respectively. We also find a minor-to-major axis ratio of the SIE component (0.34), smaller than that of the light distribution suggested by the <em>g</em>-band model result (0.85). The lensing velocity dispersion suggests that cluster or line of sight structures also contribute a substantial fraction of convergence. There is no clear evidence of a crowded environment around the ETG, either by visual inspection of color images or in the SDSS photometric redshifts, but <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn81.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim 1^{\\prime} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim 1^{\\prime}</script></span></span> to the north there is a galaxy, SDSS J142953.71+120333.9, with a BOSS spectroscopic redshift <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn82.gif\" alt=\"$z=0.5527\\pm 0.0002$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=0.5527\\pm 0.0002</script></span></span>, very close to the lensing ETG, indicating that a cluster or group of galaxies at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn83.gif\" alt=\"$z\\simeq 0.55$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\simeq 0.55</script></span></span> may be present, as suggested by the external shear field.</p><p>For the source, the lens model gives local magnifications of 3.2, 3.1, 1.8, and 0.7 for images A, B, C, and D, respectively, which means that the total magnification is 8.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.4. The source has an effective radius <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn84.gif\" alt=\"${R}_{\\mathrm{eff}}=0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 159\\pm 0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 007$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{R}_{\\mathrm{eff}}=0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 159\\pm 0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 007</script></span></span>, which corresponds to <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn85.gif\" alt=\"${R}_{\\mathrm{eff}}=1.28\\pm 0.06\\,\\mathrm{kpc}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{R}_{\\mathrm{eff}}=1.28\\pm 0.06\\,\\mathrm{kpc}</script></span></span> for the adopted cosmology. The source has a minor-to-major axis ratio <em>q</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.56 and a S\u00e9rsic index <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn86.gif\" alt=\"$n=3.9$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">n=3.9</script></span></span>. It is centered at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn87.gif\" alt=\"${\\rm{\\Delta }}{\\rm{R}}.{\\rm{A}}.\\,=\\,-0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 43$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\rm{\\Delta }}{\\rm{R}}.{\\rm{A}}.\\,=\\,-0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 43</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn88.gif\" alt=\"${\\rm{\\Delta }}\\mathrm{decl}.\\,=\\,0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 56$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\rm{\\Delta }}\\mathrm{decl}.\\,=\\,0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 56</script></span></span> relative to the center of the lens galaxy.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjlaa5591s3-3\" name=\"apjlaa5591s3-3\">3.3.\u00a0Intrinsic Properties</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Having determined the magnification of the LAE we can estimate its intrinsic properties. From the total DECaLS DR2 <em>r</em>-band magnitude, we determine a rest-frame 1600 \u00c5 luminosity <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn89.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{1600}=(6.12\\pm 0.48)\\times {10}^{30}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{1600}=(6.12\\pm 0.48)\\times {10}^{30}</script></span></span> erg s<sup>\u22121</sup> Hz<sup>\u22121</sup>. Using Kennicutt's conversion (Kennicutt <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib15\">1998</a>), this rest-frame UV luminosity translates into an intrinsic star formation rate (SFR) of <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />90 <em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub> yr<sup>\u22121</sup> when corrected for magnification, reddening, and the lower proportion of low-mass stars in the Chabrier (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib8\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib8\">2003</a>) stellar IMF relative to the standard Salpeter (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib29\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib29\">1955</a>) adopted by Kennicutt (a factor of 1/1.8). Turning to Ly<em>\u03b1</em>, assuming the space distribution of Ly<em>\u03b1</em> in the source plane and its lensing magnification are similar to that of the rest-frame UV continuum, and applying the correction for the magnification and the slit losses (the GTC/OSIRIS slit captured a fraction <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />0.60 of the total light of BG1429+1202), we derive an intrinsic Ly<em>\u03b1</em> luminosity of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn90.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=(2.80\\pm 0.39)\\,\\times {10}^{43}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=(2.80\\pm 0.39)\\,\\times {10}^{43}</script></span></span> erg s<sup>\u22121</sup>. Assuming case-B recombination and Kennicutt's conversion (Kennicutt <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib15\">1998</a>), this luminosity results in\u00a0 <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn91.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{SFR}(\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha )\\simeq 25$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{SFR}(\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha )\\simeq 25</script></span></span> <em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>. Comparing the estimates of SFR from the rest-frame UV and Ly<em>\u03b1</em>, we measure <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn92.gif\" alt=\"${f}_{\\mathrm{esc}}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim 0.30$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{f}_{\\mathrm{esc}}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim 0.30</script></span></span>, consistent with that estimated from LAEs at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn93.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> (e.g., Verhamme et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib39\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib39\">2008</a>; Zheng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib43\">2016</a>). However, we should note that the measured <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn94.gif\" alt=\"${f}_{\\mathrm{esc}}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{f}_{\\mathrm{esc}}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }</script></span></span> results from the assumption that the spatial distribution of Ly<em>\u03b1</em> (and its magnification) follows the rest-frame UV continuum. Ly<em>\u03b1</em> halos are hard to resolve from individual LAEs, and have been studied mainly by using stacking techniques (Steidel et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib38\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib38\">2011</a>; Momose et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib18\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib18\">2016</a>), or in nearby high-redshift analogs (e.g., Yang et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib40\">2016</a>). However, for a few cases, strong gravitational lensing allows spatially resolved studies of high-redshift galaxies (e.g., Patr\u00edcio et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib21\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib21\">2016</a>). A more detailed analysis will be possible with high-resolution narrowband imaging and integral field spectroscopy.</p><p>In order to establish how typical the intrinsic properties of this galaxy are, we compare it with other UV-selected <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn95.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> LBGs and LAEs. BG1429+1202 is intrinsically more luminous in the rest-frame UV by factors of 7 and 19, relative to <em>L</em><sup>*</sup> from the luminosity functions of Reddy &amp; Steidel (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib27\">2009</a>) for <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn96.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> LBGs and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn97.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3.1$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3.1</script></span></span> LAEs selected by narrowband imaging by Ouchi et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib20\">2008</a>), respectively. It is also intrinsically very luminous in <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn98.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> emission, when compared with <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn99.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{* }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{* }</script></span></span> from the luminosity functions of LAEs at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn100.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3.1$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3.1</script></span></span> (factor of ~5; Ouchi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib20\">2008</a>) and LAEs at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn101.gif\" alt=\"$z=2.8$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2.8</script></span></span> in CDFS (factor of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn102.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim 9-5;$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim 9-5;</script></span></span> Zheng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib43\">2016</a>).</p><p>Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjlaa5591t2\">2</a> presents a comparison with other well known, exceptionally bright in the optical, galaxy\u2013galaxy <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn103.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> lenses: the Cosmic Eye (Smail et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib37\">2007</a>), MS 1512-cB58 (Yee et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib41\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib41\">1996</a>), the 8 o'clock (Allam et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib1\">2007</a>), and at lower redshift, the Cosmic Horseshoe (Belokurov et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib2\">2007</a>). BG1429+1202 has similar brightness but is intrinsically very luminous in the rest-frame UV continuum and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn104.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span>. It is also the only <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn105.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> emitter (the <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn106.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> line of the Cosmic Horseshoe galaxy shares many of the properties of the <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn107.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> emitters, but its <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn108.gif\" alt=\"${W}_{0}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{W}_{0}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }</script></span></span> is below the threshold generally adopted to define it as <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn109.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> emitter; Quider et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib25\">2009</a>). This puts BG1429+1202 in the small group of very bright <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn110.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> galaxies that, due to high magnification and high intrinsic luminosity, have brightnesses that provide the unique opportunity to obtain high S/N spectroscopy, which allows us to study its physical properties in detail.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjlaa5591t2\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">5.8</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">8</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<p><strong>Notes.</strong></p>\n<a name=\"apjlaa5591t2fna\" id=\"apjlaa5591t2fna\"></a><sup> a</sup>Rest-frame UV apparent magnitudes from the <em>r</em>- or <em>i</em>-bands, depending on the redshift.\n<a name=\"apjlaa5591t2fnb\" id=\"apjlaa5591t2fnb\"></a><sup> b</sup>Total magnification factor.\n<a name=\"apjlaa5591t2fnc\" id=\"apjlaa5591t2fnc\"></a><sup> c</sup>Intrinsic rest-frame UV and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn118.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> luminosity, respectively, corrected from the lensing magnification.\n<p><strong>References.</strong> (1) Ellingson et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib13\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib13\">1996</a>), (2) Seitz et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib31\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib31\">1998</a>), (3) Smail et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib37\">2007</a>), (4) Allam et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib1\">2007</a>), (5) Belokurov et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib2\">2007</a>), (6) Quider et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib25\">2009</a>), (7) Reddy &amp; Steidel (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib27\">2009</a>), (8) Ouchi et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib20\">2008</a>).</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/suppdata/apjlaa5591t2_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/2041-8213/834/2/L18\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/suppdata/apjlaa5591t2_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa5591s4\" name=\"apjlaa5591s4\">4.\u00a0Conclusion</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>In this Letter, we report the discovery of a bright quadruply lensed LAE at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn119.gif\" alt=\"$z=2.8224$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2.8224</script></span></span>. The very bright apparent magnitude partially results from gravitational lensing by a <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn120.gif\" alt=\"$z=0.5531$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=0.5531</script></span></span> luminous red galaxy, which provides a magnification of 8.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.4. After accounting for the lensing magnification, BG1429+1202 is also intrinsically very luminous in the rest-frame UV and Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission by about 19 and 5 times the typical <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn121.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{\\mathrm{UV}}^{* }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{\\mathrm{UV}}^{* }</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn122.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{* }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{* }</script></span></span> of LAEs at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn123.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span>, respectively, showing low dust content and indications of massive recent star formation. Compared with the few well known strongly lensed galaxies, it is the most luminous one in the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> line. This makes this source another good laboratory for further detailed studies of the physics of star formation and Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission in galaxies during the cosmic epoch of star formation. The new method presented in Shu et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib34\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib34\">2016a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib35\">2016b</a>) and in this work opens a new window into the study of high-redshift galaxies using the combination of massive spectroscopic surveys, large-area multi-band imaging, gravitational lensing, and follow-up with 10 m telescopes like GTC.</p></div> <div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We thank the anonymous referee for helpful comments. We thank the IAC Director for the allocation of WHT and GTC discretionary time and the WHT and GTC staff for efficient support and fast completion of the two DDT programs. R.M.C. acknowledges Fundaci\u00f3n La Caixa for the financial support received in the form of a PhD contract. This work was funded in part by the project ESP2015-65597-C4-4-R of the Spanish Ministerio de Econom\u00eda y Competitividad (MINECO). S.M. and Y.S. acknowledge the support by the Strategic Priority Research Program \"The Emergence of Cosmological Structures\" of the Chinese Academy of Sciences Grant No. XDB09000000 and by the National Natural Science Foundation of China (NSFC) under grant numbers 11333003, 11390372, and 11603032. Funding for SDSS-III has been provided by the Alfred P. Sloan Foundation, the Participating Institutions, the National Science Foundation, and the U.S. Department of Energy Office of Science. The SDSS-III web site is <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"webref\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"http://www.sdss3.org/\">http://www.sdss3.org/</a>.</p></div></div><!-- End article <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">2041-8205/834/2/L18</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n            <P>We report the discovery of a very bright (<I>r</I>\u00a0=\u00a020.16), highly magnified, and yet intrinsically very luminous Ly<I>\u03b1</I> emitter (LAE) at <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$z=2.82$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/apjlaa5591ieqn1.gif\"></IMG>. This system comprises four images in the observer plane with a maximum separation of <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$\\sim 6^{\\prime\\prime} $\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/apjlaa5591ieqn2.gif\"></IMG> and it is lensed by a <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$z=0.55$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/apjlaa5591ieqn3.gif\"></IMG> massive early-type galaxy. It was initially identified in the Baryon Oscillation Spectroscopic Survey Emission-Line Lens Survey for GALaxy-Ly<I>\u03b1</I> EmitteR sYstems survey, and follow-up imaging and spectroscopic observations using the Gran Telescopio Canarias and William Herschel Telescope confirmed the lensing nature of this system. A lens model using a singular isothermal ellipsoid in an external shear field reproduces the main features of the system quite well, yielding an Einstein radius of 2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />95\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />10, and a total magnification factor for the LAE of 8.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.4. This LAE is one of the brightest and most luminous galaxy\u2013galaxy strong lenses known. We present initial imaging and spectroscopy showing the basic physical and morphological properties of this lensed system.</P></div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=2041-8205/834/2/L18&doi=10.3847/2041-8213/834/2/L18&exportFormat=iopexport_bib&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-bib\" title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=2041-8205/834/2/L18&doi=10.3847/2041-8213/834/2/L18&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-ris\" title=\"Export RIS\">RIS</a>\n\t\t</span>\n\t</p>\n<!-- End Export citation and abstract tools -->\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2017ApJ...834L..18M\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://nedwww.ipac.caltech.edu/cgi-bin/nph-objsearch?refcode=2017ApJ...834L..18M&search_type=Search \" target=\"_blank\">NED Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2017ApJ...834L..18M\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/2041-8205/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa5591s1\" name=\"apjlaa5591s1\">1.\u00a0Introduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The study of the physical properties of typical <em>L</em>* high-redshift galaxies has been limited by their faintness (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn4.gif\" alt=\"$r\\simeq 24.5$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">r\\simeq 24.5</script></span></span> at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn5.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span>), even for 8/10 m class telescopes. Recently, the properties of these high-redshift galaxies have been studied by building large samples of hundreds to thousands of individual spectra to construct high signal-to-noise ratio (S/N) composite spectra (e.g., Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib32\">2003</a>). Although these techniques have been very successful, they require a large amount of observing time and only probe the average physical properties of these galaxies. Another way to study high-redshift galaxies in detail is to use the fortuitous alignments with foreground massive structures, which provide natural magnification and associated amplification produced by strong gravitational lensing. Hundreds of strongly lensed galaxies have recently been discovered by employing various observational techniques, mainly from the optical to the radio. However, only a handful of optically very bright (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn6.gif\" alt=\"$r\\sim 20$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">r\\sim 20</script></span></span>), strongly magnified high-redshift galaxies have been discovered so far (Yee et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib41\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib41\">1996</a>; Allam et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib1\">2007</a>; Belokurov et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib2\">2007</a>; Smail et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib37\">2007</a>; Lin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib17\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib17\">2009</a>; Dahle et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib9\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib9\">2016</a>), allowing detailed spectroscopic studies of their individual properties, such as stellar populations, chemical composition, and kinematics of the interstellar medium (e.g., Pettini et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib24\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib24\">2000</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib23\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib23\">2002</a>; Quider et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib25\">2009</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib26\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib26\">2010</a>; Dessauges-Zavadsky et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib11\">2010</a>).</p><p>In this Letter, we report the discovery of a bright (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn7.gif\" alt=\"$r\\sim 20$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">r\\sim 20</script></span></span>), quadruply gravitationally lensed Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emitter (LAE). We provide the first physical and morphological analysis of the lensing galaxy and the lensed LAE. Throughout the Letter, we adopt a cosmology with <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn8.gif\" alt=\"${{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{m}}}=0.274$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{m}}}=0.274</script></span></span>, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn9.gif\" alt=\"${{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{\\Lambda }}}=0.726$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{\\Lambda }}}=0.726</script></span></span> and <em>H</em><sub><em>o</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a070 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. All quoted magnitudes are in the AB system.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa5591s2\" name=\"apjlaa5591s2\">2.\u00a0Discovery and Follow-up</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Recently, by searching for secondary emission lines in the spectra of massive elliptical galaxies within the database of the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS: York et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib42\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib42\">2000</a>), the Sloan Lens ACS Survey (SLACS: e.g., Bolton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib5\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib5\">2006</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib4\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib4\">2008</a>), and the Baryon Oscillation Spectroscopic Survey (BOSS) Emission-Line Lens Survey (BELLS: Brownstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib6\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib6\">2012</a>) have discovered over 100 lensed star-forming galaxies at moderate redshifts (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn10.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 1$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 1</script></span></span>). Very recently, by applying spectroscopic selection techniques similar to SLACS and BELLS, but adapted to high-redshift Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission, Shu et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib34\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib34\">2016a</a>) identified a new sample of 187 high-probability lensed LAE candidate systems at 2 &lt; <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn11.gif\" alt=\"${z}_{\\mathrm{LAE}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{z}_{\\mathrm{LAE}}</script></span></span> &lt; 3, the BOSS Emission-Line Lens Survey for GALaxy-Ly<em>\u03b1</em> EmitteR sYstems (BELLS GALLERY) survey, selected from the final data release (DR12) of the BOSS (Dawson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib10\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib10\">2013</a>) of the SDSS-III (Eisenstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib12\">2011</a>). Of these, 21 of the highest quality candidates were recently observed with the <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> and the first results were presented in Shu et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib35\">2016b</a>).</p><p>By visual inspection of SDSS and DECaLS<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa5591fn2\">12</a></sup>\n color images of the BELLS GALLERY sample, we found one candidate showing bluish features <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />3<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />3 from the <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn12.gif\" alt=\"$z=0.5531$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=0.5531</script></span></span> massive early-type galaxy, SDSS J142954.80+120235.6 (hereafter ETG). Its BOSS spectrum (Plate-MJD-Fiber: 5463-56003-121) shows a secondary emission line at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn13.gif\" alt=\"$4652\\,\\mathring{\\rm A} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">4652\\,\\mathring{\\rm A}</script></span></span> (Ly<em>\u03b1</em> at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn14.gif\" alt=\"$z=2.8253;$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2.8253;</script></span></span> Shu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib34\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib34\">2016a</a>). The positions of the bluish features with respect to the ETG are consistent with a <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn15.gif\" alt=\"${\\text{}}{fold}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\text{}}{fold}</script></span></span> lensing configuration: a bright lensed image pair, A and B (with a separation of <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5), and two fainter images, C and D (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>). The lensed image pair, A and B, is identified in SDSS as a single source, SDSS J142954.88+120238.3 (hereafter BG1429+1202 for the lensed LAE, where BG stands for BELLS GALLERY), showing blue colors in the DECaLS and SDSS bands (Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjlaa5591t1\">1</a>). The lensed A and B images are also detected in the UKIRT Infrared Deep Sky\u00a0 Large Area Survey (Lawrence et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib16\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib16\">2007</a>), only in the <em>Y</em>-band with 21.06\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.19 mag and 21.12\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.20 mag, respectively.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjlaa5591f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjlaa5591f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">(5)</script></span></span> the lensed images A and B were deblended using <span class=\"small-caps\">GALFIT</span> (Peng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib22\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib22\">2002</a>). The magnitudes listed have not been corrected for the Galactic dust extinction, which are 0.104, 0.072, and 0.040 mag for <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, and <em>z</em>, respectively (Schlafly &amp; Finkbeiner <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib30\">2011</a>).</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/suppdata/apjlaa5591t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/2041-8213/834/2/L18\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/suppdata/apjlaa5591t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>We carried out Director Discretionary Time (DDT) for optical imaging and long-slit spectroscopic observations on 2016 June 29 using the Auxiliary-port Camera (ACAM: Benn et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib3\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib3\">2008</a>) at the William Herschel Telescope (WHT) to confirm the lensing nature of this LAE. The ACAM long-slit was oriented at a sky position angle (PA)\u00a0=\u00a0<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn32.gif\" alt=\"$103\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 35$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">103\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 35</script></span></span>, and positioned so as to encompass the two brightest lensed images, A and B, as shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>. Despite the bad seeing conditions that night (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn33.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim 4^{\\prime\\prime} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim 4^{\\prime\\prime}</script></span></span> FWHM), we could confirm the lensing nature of this system with the detection in the long-slit spectrum of strong rest-frame UV continuum (with Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> and C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> in absorption) and Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission at a redshift <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn34.gif\" alt=\"$z=2.823\\pm 0.008$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2.823\\pm 0.008</script></span></span>, in agreement with the redshift of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> detected in the BOSS fiber spectrum, likely from the lensed image D (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>).</p><p>We again observed BG1429+1202 on 2016 July 29, this time in very good seeing conditions (<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />75 FWHM, measured in the 330 s <em>g</em>-band acquisition image), using the Optical System for Imaging and low-Intermediate-Resolution Integrated Spectroscopy camera (OSIRIS<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa5591fn3\">13</a></sup>\n) on the Gran Telescopio Canarias (GTC). We used the R1000B grism, which provides a spectral coverage of 3630\u20137500 \u00c5 (950\u20131960 \u00c5, rest-frame) and a dispersion of 2.12 \u00c5 px<sup>\u22121</sup>. The OSIRIS <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn35.gif\" alt=\"$1\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 2</script></span></span> wide long-slit was oriented in the same PA used in the WHT/ACAM spectroscopic observations (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>). Given this configuration, the corresponding spectral resolution is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn36.gif\" alt=\"$\\simeq 8\\,\\mathring{\\rm A} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\simeq 8\\,\\mathring{\\rm A}</script></span></span> (or <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn37.gif\" alt=\"$\\simeq 500$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\simeq 500</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup> FWHM). The total integration time was 44 minutes, split into 4\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a0660 s. The data were reduced with <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span> and <span class=\"small-caps\">python</span> tasks.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa5591s3\" name=\"apjlaa5591s3\">3.\u00a0Analysis and Discussion</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjlaa5591s3-1\" name=\"apjlaa5591s3-1\">3.1.\u00a0Source Properties</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The rest-frame UV spectrum of the brightest lensed images, A and B, is shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f2\">2</a>. Despite the relatively short exposure time, the achieved high S/N GTC/OSIRIS spectrum (~25 in the continuum) shows a strong Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission, and a series of strong absorption lines, similar to those seen in the composite spectrum of hundreds of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn38.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> Lyman break galaxies (LBGs) (Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib32\">2003</a>). The strongest absorption features are associated with the interstellar medium and stellar winds in a variety of ionization states, from neutral (O <span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>) to highly ionized species (Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> or C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>). High ionization features with a strong P Cygni profile are seen both in C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn39.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1548$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1548</script></span></span>, 1550 and Al <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn40.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1854$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1854</script></span></span>, 1862 doublets, which is indicative of stellar winds from very young massive stars. However, we identify additional absorption features unrelated to BG1429+1202 (nine absorption features associated with an intervening metal-line system at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn41.gif\" alt=\"${z}_{\\mathrm{abs}}=2.179\\pm 0.001$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{z}_{\\mathrm{abs}}=2.179\\pm 0.001</script></span></span>, and one broad absorption line at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn42.gif\" alt=\"$5183\\,\\mathring{\\rm A} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">5183\\,\\mathring{\\rm A}</script></span></span> with an observed equivalent width <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn43.gif\" alt=\"${W}_{\\mathrm{obs}}=6.95\\pm 0.2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{W}_{\\mathrm{obs}}=6.95\\pm 0.2</script></span></span> \u00c5 remains unidentified). Analysis of the spectra for the individual lensed images A and B shows no differences in the profiles of the absorption features and no evidence for velocity offsets between them, as expected if they are both images of the same background source. The same happens to their rest-frame UV slope, <em>\u03b2</em>, which is essentially flat in <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn44.gif\" alt=\"${F}_{\\nu }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{F}_{\\nu }</script></span></span>. Adopting a simple power-law approximation for the UV spectral range <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn45.gif\" alt=\"${F}_{\\lambda }\\propto {\\lambda }^{\\beta }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{F}_{\\lambda }\\propto {\\lambda }^{\\beta }</script></span></span> and using the observed <em>r</em> and <em>z</em> magnitudes (~1600\u20132400 \u00c5 rest-frame), we derive <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn46.gif\" alt=\"$\\beta =-2.1\\pm 0.1$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\beta =-2.1\\pm 0.1</script></span></span>, which implies an effective UV extinction <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn47.gif\" alt=\"${A}_{1600}\\sim 0.6$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{A}_{1600}\\sim 0.6</script></span></span> or <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn48.gif\" alt=\"$E(B-V)\\sim 0.13$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)\\sim 0.13</script></span></span>, reflecting modest dust content (Calzetti et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib7\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib7\">2000</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjlaa5591f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjlaa5591f2\" 2.</strong>\u00a0GTC/OSIRIS spectrum of BG1429+1202 (black solid line) and its <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn49.gif\" alt=\"$1\\sigma $\" The 2D spectrum is also shown on the top. In the inset panel we show the BOSS and WHT spectra with the positions of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission, as well as the absorption features related to the ETG at <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span
