from the BOSS fiber spectrum.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjlaa5591f2\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/downloadFigure/figure/apjlaa5591f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjlaa5591f2\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjlaa5591f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>We identified several photospheric absorption features, from which we derived the systemic redshift <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn51.gif\" alt=\"${z}_{\\mathrm{sys}}=2.8224\\,\\pm \\,0.0013$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{z}_{\\mathrm{sys}}=2.8224\\,\\pm \\,0.0013</script></span></span> using the cleanest among them: O <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn52.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1343$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1343</script></span></span>, and a close blend of C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and N <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span> at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn53.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1324$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1324</script></span></span>.</p><p>The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission line has an observed (A + B) flux of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn54.gif\" alt=\"${F}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=(2.1\\pm 0.3)\\times {10}^{-15}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{F}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=(2.1\\pm 0.3)\\times {10}^{-15}</script></span></span> erg s<sup>\u22121</sup> cm<sup>\u22122</sup>, much higher than the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> flux measured within the <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn55.gif\" alt=\"$1^{\\prime\\prime} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1^{\\prime\\prime}</script></span></span>-radius BOSS fiber (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn56.gif\" alt=\"${F}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{\\mathrm{BOSS}}=0.256\\times {10}^{-15}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{F}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{\\mathrm{BOSS}}=0.256\\times {10}^{-15}</script></span></span> erg s<sup>\u22121</sup> cm<sup>\u22122</sup>). The measured rest-frame equivalent width of Ly<em>\u03b1</em> is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn57.gif\" alt=\"${W}_{0}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=39\\pm 15$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{W}_{0}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=39\\pm 15</script></span></span> \u00c5. The errors reflect the uncertainty in the determination of the stellar continuum redward of Ly<em>\u03b1</em>. Although the line appears unresolved in our low-resolution spectrum (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn58.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{FWHM}\\simeq 500$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{FWHM}\\simeq 500</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup>), it is resolved in the BOSS spectrum. Fitting a Gaussian to the BOSS Ly<em>\u03b1</em> line, we measured a FWHM of 382\u00a0\u00b1\u00a050 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, after accounting for the instrumental broadening. The nebular C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii]</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn59.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1906$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1906</script></span></span>, 1908 doublet is also detected in emission but with low significance (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn60.gif\" alt=\"$4\\sigma $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">4\\sigma</script></span></span>) and is not resolved in our GTC/OSIRIS spectrum. This galaxy can be classified as an LAE, given the rest-frame equivalent width and the velocity width of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> line (e.g., Ouchi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib20\">2008</a>). From our spectrum and available photometric data we do not detect evidence of any AGN contribution. However, a more extensive characterization awaits higher spatial resolution imaging and multi-wavelength photometry.</p><p>A careful analysis of the kinematics goes beyond the present Letter given the low spectral resolution of these data. However, the high S/N of the GTC/OSIRIS spectrum allows us to detect differences in the kinematics of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission and interstellar features. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f3\">3</a> (left panel) shows velocity plots of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission line and several normalized interstellar absorption lines, relative to <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn61.gif\" alt=\"${z}_{\\mathrm{sys}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{z}_{\\mathrm{sys}}</script></span></span>. The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission has its peak redshifted with a velocity <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn62.gif\" alt=\"${v}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim +200$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{v}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim +200</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, while the interstellar absorption lines appear blueshifted by <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn63.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim -150$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim -150</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, which is consistent with galaxy-scale outflows of material from the galaxy in the form of a wind, similar to those seen in other star-forming galaxies at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn64.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> (Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib32\">2003</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjlaa5591f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjlaa5591f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591f3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0Left: GTC/OSIRIS and BOSS Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission (upper panel) and interstellar absorption features (lower panel) on rest velocity frame. The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission appears to be redshifted, <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn65.gif\" alt=\"${v}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim +200$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{v}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim +200</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, while the interstellar absorption lines are blueshifted by <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn66.gif\" alt=\"${v}_{\\mathrm{abs}}\\sim -150$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{v}_{\\mathrm{abs}}\\sim -150</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup> (mean profile in black with the standard deviation in gray shadow). Right: 2D Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission in the position\u2013velocity plane (upper panel) where a spatial gradient of velocity is seen in both A and B images. In the lower panel we show the normalized spatial profiles of the rest-frame UV continuum (green line) and Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission (blue line). The shaded regions show the <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn67.gif\" alt=\"$1\\sigma $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1\\sigma</script></span></span> errors of the spatial profiles. The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission appears more extended between A and B than the rest-frame UV continuum.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjlaa5591f3\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/downloadFigure/figure/apjlaa5591f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjlaa5591f3\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjlaa5591f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>We also notice that a spatial gradient of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> velocity is present in the 2D spectrum (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f3\">3</a>, right upper panel). This velocity structure is seen both in A and B but appears mirrored, as expected for those images in this system, as A and B images straddle the fold critical curve (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>). We carefully checked the 2D spectrum to see if this pattern is present in other lines, but we found none with this signature. The 1D spatial distribution of Ly<em>\u03b1</em> is also compared with that of the rest-frame UV continuum (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f3\">3</a>, right lower panel). The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission appears more extended in the inner region between A and B, than the UV continuum. Deeper and higher spatial resolution observations are needed to constrain the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> and UV continuum spatial distributions.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjlaa5591s3-2\" name=\"apjlaa5591s3-2\">3.2.\u00a0Lens Model</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>To interpret the properties of the lensed system in more detail, we used the 330 s GTC/OSIRIS <em>g</em>-band image obtained in <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn68.gif\" alt=\"$\\simeq 0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 75$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\simeq 0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 75</script></span></span> FWHM seeing for accurate lens modeling. As shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa5591f1\">1</a>, the lens system comprises four images forming a so-called <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn69.gif\" alt=\"${\\text{}}{fold}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\text{}}{fold}</script></span></span> configuration, when the source lies very close to a <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn70.gif\" alt=\"${\\text{}}{fold}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\text{}}{fold}</script></span></span> caustic. Similar to previous works (Bolton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib4\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib4\">2008</a>; Brownstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib6\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib6\">2012</a>; Shu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib33\">2015</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib35\">2016b</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib36\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib36\">2016c</a>), we have developed a lens model using a nonlinear optimizer, consisting of minimizing a <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn71.gif\" alt=\"${\\chi }^{2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\chi }^{2}</script></span></span> function using the Levenberg\u2013Marquardt algorithm with the <tt>LMFIT</tt> package (Newville et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib19\">2014</a>), where the observational data are compared to the model (see Shu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib35\">2016b</a> for details). The foreground-light is modeled using the elliptical S\u00e9rsic profile and similar to Shu et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib33\">2015</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib35\">2016b</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib36\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib36\">2016c</a>), its subtraction is performed jointly with the lens modeling. The lens model includes a mass distribution of the foreground lens parameterized as a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE), and an additional external shear is included to model the higher-order effect from the environment. The surface brightness distribution of the background source is reconstructed parametrically using an elliptical S\u00e9rsic model. The foreground-light model is combined with the predicted lensed images and convolved with the point-spread function that was modeled with a star in the GTC/OSIRIS <em>g</em>-band field of view.</p><p>For the lens, the best-fit lens model (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn72.gif\" alt=\"${\\chi }^{2}/\\mathrm{dof}=3494/3709$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\chi }^{2}/\\mathrm{dof}=3494/3709</script></span></span>) predicts an Einstein radius <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn73.gif\" alt=\"${b}_{\\mathrm{SIE}}=2\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 95\\,\\pm \\,0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 10$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{b}_{\\mathrm{SIE}}=2\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 95\\,\\pm \\,0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 10</script></span></span>, a minor-to-major axis ratio <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn74.gif\" alt=\"$q=0.34$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">q=0.34</script></span></span>, and a position angle <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn75.gif\" alt=\"${\\rm{P}}.{\\rm{A}}.\\,=\\,165\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 5$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\rm{P}}.{\\rm{A}}.\\,=\\,165\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 5</script></span></span>. The strength and position angle of the external shear are <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn76.gif\" alt=\"$\\gamma =0.059\\pm 0.008$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\gamma =0.059\\pm 0.008</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn77.gif\" alt=\"${\\phi }_{\\gamma }=89\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 9$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\phi }_{\\gamma }=89\\buildrel{\\circ}\\over{.} 9</script></span></span>, respectively. The characteristic lensing velocity dispersion defined as <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn78.gif\" alt=\"${\\sigma }_{\\mathrm{SIE}}=c\\sqrt{\\tfrac{{b}_{\\mathrm{SIE}}}{4\\pi }\\tfrac{{D}_{{\\rm{L}}}}{{D}_{\\mathrm{LS}}}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\sigma }_{\\mathrm{SIE}}=c\\sqrt{\\tfrac{{b}_{\\mathrm{SIE}}}{4\\pi }\\tfrac{{D}_{{\\rm{L}}}}{{D}_{\\mathrm{LS}}}}</script></span></span> is 390\u00a0\u00b1\u00a06 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, where <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn79.gif\" alt=\"${D}_{\\mathrm{LS}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{D}_{\\mathrm{LS}}</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn80.gif\" alt=\"${D}_{{\\rm{S}}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{D}_{{\\rm{S}}}</script></span></span> are the angular diameter distances from the lens and the observer to the source, respectively. We also find a minor-to-major axis ratio of the SIE component (0.34), smaller than that of the light distribution suggested by the <em>g</em>-band model result (0.85). The lensing velocity dispersion suggests that cluster or line of sight structures also contribute a substantial fraction of convergence. There is no clear evidence of a crowded environment around the ETG, either by visual inspection of color images or in the SDSS photometric redshifts, but <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn81.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim 1^{\\prime} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim 1^{\\prime}</script></span></span> to the north there is a galaxy, SDSS J142953.71+120333.9, with a BOSS spectroscopic redshift <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn82.gif\" alt=\"$z=0.5527\\pm 0.0002$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=0.5527\\pm 0.0002</script></span></span>, very close to the lensing ETG, indicating that a cluster or group of galaxies at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn83.gif\" alt=\"$z\\simeq 0.55$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\simeq 0.55</script></span></span> may be present, as suggested by the external shear field.</p><p>For the source, the lens model gives local magnifications of 3.2, 3.1, 1.8, and 0.7 for images A, B, C, and D, respectively, which means that the total magnification is 8.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.4. The source has an effective radius <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn84.gif\" alt=\"${R}_{\\mathrm{eff}}=0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 159\\pm 0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 007$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{R}_{\\mathrm{eff}}=0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 159\\pm 0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 007</script></span></span>, which corresponds to <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn85.gif\" alt=\"${R}_{\\mathrm{eff}}=1.28\\pm 0.06\\,\\mathrm{kpc}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{R}_{\\mathrm{eff}}=1.28\\pm 0.06\\,\\mathrm{kpc}</script></span></span> for the adopted cosmology. The source has a minor-to-major axis ratio <em>q</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.56 and a S\u00e9rsic index <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn86.gif\" alt=\"$n=3.9$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">n=3.9</script></span></span>. It is centered at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn87.gif\" alt=\"${\\rm{\\Delta }}{\\rm{R}}.{\\rm{A}}.\\,=\\,-0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 43$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\rm{\\Delta }}{\\rm{R}}.{\\rm{A}}.\\,=\\,-0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 43</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn88.gif\" alt=\"${\\rm{\\Delta }}\\mathrm{decl}.\\,=\\,0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 56$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\rm{\\Delta }}\\mathrm{decl}.\\,=\\,0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 56</script></span></span> relative to the center of the lens galaxy.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjlaa5591s3-3\" name=\"apjlaa5591s3-3\">3.3.\u00a0Intrinsic Properties</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Having determined the magnification of the LAE we can estimate its intrinsic properties. From the total DECaLS DR2 <em>r</em>-band magnitude, we determine a rest-frame 1600 \u00c5 luminosity <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn89.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{1600}=(6.12\\pm 0.48)\\times {10}^{30}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{1600}=(6.12\\pm 0.48)\\times {10}^{30}</script></span></span> erg s<sup>\u22121</sup> Hz<sup>\u22121</sup>. Using Kennicutt's conversion (Kennicutt <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib15\">1998</a>), this rest-frame UV luminosity translates into an intrinsic star formation rate (SFR) of <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />90 <em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub> yr<sup>\u22121</sup> when corrected for magnification, reddening, and the lower proportion of low-mass stars in the Chabrier (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib8\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib8\">2003</a>) stellar IMF relative to the standard Salpeter (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib29\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib29\">1955</a>) adopted by Kennicutt (a factor of 1/1.8). Turning to Ly<em>\u03b1</em>, assuming the space distribution of Ly<em>\u03b1</em> in the source plane and its lensing magnification are similar to that of the rest-frame UV continuum, and applying the correction for the magnification and the slit losses (the GTC/OSIRIS slit captured a fraction <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />0.60 of the total light of BG1429+1202), we derive an intrinsic Ly<em>\u03b1</em> luminosity of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn90.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=(2.80\\pm 0.39)\\,\\times {10}^{43}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }=(2.80\\pm 0.39)\\,\\times {10}^{43}</script></span></span> erg s<sup>\u22121</sup>. Assuming case-B recombination and Kennicutt's conversion (Kennicutt <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib15\">1998</a>), this luminosity results in\u00a0 <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn91.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{SFR}(\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha )\\simeq 25$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{SFR}(\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha )\\simeq 25</script></span></span> <em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>. Comparing the estimates of SFR from the rest-frame UV and Ly<em>\u03b1</em>, we measure <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn92.gif\" alt=\"${f}_{\\mathrm{esc}}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim 0.30$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{f}_{\\mathrm{esc}}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }\\sim 0.30</script></span></span>, consistent with that estimated from LAEs at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn93.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> (e.g., Verhamme et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib39\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib39\">2008</a>; Zheng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib43\">2016</a>). However, we should note that the measured <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn94.gif\" alt=\"${f}_{\\mathrm{esc}}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{f}_{\\mathrm{esc}}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }</script></span></span> results from the assumption that the spatial distribution of Ly<em>\u03b1</em> (and its magnification) follows the rest-frame UV continuum. Ly<em>\u03b1</em> halos are hard to resolve from individual LAEs, and have been studied mainly by using stacking techniques (Steidel et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib38\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib38\">2011</a>; Momose et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib18\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib18\">2016</a>), or in nearby high-redshift analogs (e.g., Yang et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib40\">2016</a>). However, for a few cases, strong gravitational lensing allows spatially resolved studies of high-redshift galaxies (e.g., Patr\u00edcio et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib21\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib21\">2016</a>). A more detailed analysis will be possible with high-resolution narrowband imaging and integral field spectroscopy.</p><p>In order to establish how typical the intrinsic properties of this galaxy are, we compare it with other UV-selected <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn95.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> LBGs and LAEs. BG1429+1202 is intrinsically more luminous in the rest-frame UV by factors of 7 and 19, relative to <em>L</em><sup>*</sup> from the luminosity functions of Reddy &amp; Steidel (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib27\">2009</a>) for <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn96.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> LBGs and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn97.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3.1$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3.1</script></span></span> LAEs selected by narrowband imaging by Ouchi et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib20\">2008</a>), respectively. It is also intrinsically very luminous in <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn98.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> emission, when compared with <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn99.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{* }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{* }</script></span></span> from the luminosity functions of LAEs at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn100.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3.1$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3.1</script></span></span> (factor of ~5; Ouchi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib20\">2008</a>) and LAEs at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn101.gif\" alt=\"$z=2.8$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2.8</script></span></span> in CDFS (factor of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn102.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim 9-5;$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim 9-5;</script></span></span> Zheng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib43\">2016</a>).</p><p>Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjlaa5591t2\">2</a> presents a comparison with other well known, exceptionally bright in the optical, galaxy\u2013galaxy <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn103.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> lenses: the Cosmic Eye (Smail et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib37\">2007</a>), MS 1512-cB58 (Yee et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib41\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib41\">1996</a>), the 8 o'clock (Allam et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib1\">2007</a>), and at lower redshift, the Cosmic Horseshoe (Belokurov et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib2\">2007</a>). BG1429+1202 has similar brightness but is intrinsically very luminous in the rest-frame UV continuum and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn104.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span>. It is also the only <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn105.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> emitter (the <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn106.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> line of the Cosmic Horseshoe galaxy shares many of the properties of the <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn107.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> emitters, but its <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn108.gif\" alt=\"${W}_{0}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{W}_{0}^{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }</script></span></span> is below the threshold generally adopted to define it as <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn109.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> emitter; Quider et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib25\">2009</a>). This puts BG1429+1202 in the small group of very bright <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn110.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span> galaxies that, due to high magnification and high intrinsic luminosity, have brightnesses that provide the unique opportunity to obtain high S/N spectroscopy, which allows us to study its physical properties in detail.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjlaa5591t2\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">5.8</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">8</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<p><strong>Notes.</strong></p>\n<a name=\"apjlaa5591t2fna\" id=\"apjlaa5591t2fna\"></a><sup> a</sup>Rest-frame UV apparent magnitudes from the <em>r</em>- or <em>i</em>-bands, depending on the redshift.\n<a name=\"apjlaa5591t2fnb\" id=\"apjlaa5591t2fnb\"></a><sup> b</sup>Total magnification factor.\n<a name=\"apjlaa5591t2fnc\" id=\"apjlaa5591t2fnc\"></a><sup> c</sup>Intrinsic rest-frame UV and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn118.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha</script></span></span> luminosity, respectively, corrected from the lensing magnification.\n<p><strong>References.</strong> (1) Ellingson et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib13\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib13\">1996</a>), (2) Seitz et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib31\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib31\">1998</a>), (3) Smail et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib37\">2007</a>), (4) Allam et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib1\">2007</a>), (5) Belokurov et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib2\">2007</a>), (6) Quider et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib25\">2009</a>), (7) Reddy &amp; Steidel (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib27\">2009</a>), (8) Ouchi et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib20\">2008</a>).</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/suppdata/apjlaa5591t2_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/2041-8213/834/2/L18\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/2041-8205/834/2/L18/suppdata/apjlaa5591t2_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa5591s4\" name=\"apjlaa5591s4\">4.\u00a0Conclusion</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>In this Letter, we report the discovery of a bright quadruply lensed LAE at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn119.gif\" alt=\"$z=2.8224$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2.8224</script></span></span>. The very bright apparent magnitude partially results from gravitational lensing by a <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn120.gif\" alt=\"$z=0.5531$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=0.5531</script></span></span> luminous red galaxy, which provides a magnification of 8.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.4. After accounting for the lensing magnification, BG1429+1202 is also intrinsically very luminous in the rest-frame UV and Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission by about 19 and 5 times the typical <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn121.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{\\mathrm{UV}}^{* }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{\\mathrm{UV}}^{* }</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn122.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{* }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\alpha }^{* }</script></span></span> of LAEs at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/834/2/L18/Full/apjlaa5591ieqn123.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 3</script></span></span>, respectively, showing low dust content and indications of massive recent star formation. Compared with the few well known strongly lensed galaxies, it is the most luminous one in the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> line. This makes this source another good laboratory for further detailed studies of the physics of star formation and Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission in galaxies during the cosmic epoch of star formation. The new method presented in Shu et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib34\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib34\">2016a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa5591bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa5591bib35\">2016b</a>) and in this work opens a new window into the study of high-redshift galaxies using the combination of massive spectroscopic surveys, large-area multi-band imaging, gravitational lensing, and follow-up with 10 m telescopes like GTC.</p></div> <div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We thank the anonymous referee for helpful comments. We thank the IAC Director for the allocation of WHT and GTC discretionary time and the WHT and GTC staff for efficient support and fast completion of the two DDT programs. R.M.C. acknowledges Fundaci\u00f3n La Caixa for the financial support received in the form of a PhD contract. This work was funded in part by the project ESP2015-65597-C4-4-R of the Spanish Ministerio de Econom\u00eda y Competitividad (MINECO). S.M. and Y.S. acknowledge the support by the Strategic Priority Research Program \"The Emergence of Cosmological Structures\" of the Chinese Academy of Sciences Grant No. XDB09000000 and by the National Natural Science Foundation of China (NSFC) under grant numbers 11333003, 11390372, and 11603032. Funding for SDSS-III has been provided by the Alfred P. Sloan Foundation, the Participating Institutions, the National Science Foundation, and the U.S. Department of Energy Office of Science. The SDSS-III web site is <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"webref\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"http://www.sdss3.org/\">http://www.sdss3.org/</a>.</p></div></div><!-- End article
